✻ Worked for 5m 50s

❯ Why do you reccomend that the frontend converts. Not the backend              

● Five concrete reasons, in order of impact:

  1. Bandwidth & the 5 MB cap. A raw iPhone HEIC is 2–5 MB; base64-encoded
  that's 2.7–6.7 MB and routinely blows past CONTRACTS §4.5's 5 MB limit (and
  Vercel's default 4.5 MB request body limit on Edge). Client-side decode →
  downscale to 2048px → JPEG re-encode typically yields 200–800 KB. Backend
  conversion means the iPhone has to upload the full HEIC first, which is
  exactly what we're trying to avoid.
  2. Frontend already has to downscale. CONTRACTS already requires the frontend
  to downscale large captures to longest-edge 2048px. That decodes the image
  into a canvas, which means JPEG re-encode is a free
  canvas.toBlob("image/jpeg") — HEIC→JPEG comes essentially as a side-effect of
  work we're doing anyway. Backend conversion would add a
  decode+downscale+encode pass on top of what the frontend is already doing.
  3. Server-side HEIC is heavy on serverless. sharp needs libvips compiled with
  HEIF support. Vercel's default Node runtime doesn't ship that; you'd be
  packaging native libheif into the function bundle. That inflates cold-start
  time and bundle size on a hot path (/api/recognize) where every ms before the
  Gemini call hurts.
  4. Failure cost is lower client-side. If heic2any fails on a weird image, the
  user retakes — local error. If backend conversion fails, the user's already
  paid the upload cost and gets an opaque 4xx after several seconds.
  5. No CONTRACTS change. Frontend conversion keeps /api/recognize strictly to
  image/jpeg | png | webp. Backend conversion forces us to add image/heic to the
   contract — possible but worth avoiding for a 36-hour MVP.

  The one case backend conversion wins is if you expect non-iOS clients (Android
   Camera2 with HEIF, RAW photos, etc.). For Wellspring's iPhone-first volunteer
   app, that doesn't apply.

  Want me to re-ask Q3/Q4 now?

     Wellspring — Two-Agent Rollout Plan

     Context

     Wellspring Women's Center needs an MVP donation logger to replace a paper
     log: mobile-first volunteer app, iPad variant for every screen, Clerk auth,
      MongoDB persistence, Gemini photo recognition, soft-deletes + audit log on
      every write. Three spec docs already exist at the repo root:

     - CONTRACTS.md — wire-format middleware between agents
     - PLAN.md — phasing & file ownership
     - wellspring-build-brief.md — visual + screen spec

     Current repo state: docs only. Zero scaffolding — no src/, no package.json,
      no .env*, no .claude/. The references in PLAN.md to "the existing static
     mockup at src/app/App.tsx" and "shadcn/ui already available in
     src/app/components/ui/" do not exist; Phase 1 frontend builds routes from
     the brief's screen specs from scratch (the brief is detailed enough to do
     that).

     Goal: kick off a frontend agent and a backend agent that build in parallel,
      each treating CONTRACTS.md as the contract of record. Demo target: Vercel
     preview deploy.

     ---
     Decisions locked in this session

     #: 1
     Decision: I run Phase 0 as a single coordinator pass after plan approval
     Rationale: Atomic seed; both agents fork off cleanly with no race on shared

       scaffolding
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 2
     Decision: MongoDB Atlas M10 cluster (user-provisioned)
     Rationale: Production-grade tier, dedicated resources
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 3
     Decision: Clerk + Mongo Atlas + Gemini all live from day 1
     Rationale: No service stubs; agents wire real services from Phase 1
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 4
     Decision: All three spec docs move to src/imports/
     Rationale: Co-locates docs with code; matches the layout PLAN.md §1 already

       implies
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 5
     Decision: loggedByName / actorName stored as full name (Jessica Martinez);
     UI
       renders abbreviated (Jessica M.) via a shared helper
     Rationale: Single canonical record in DB, flexible display
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 6
     Decision: Quick Pick chips populate dynamically from /api/categories
     Rationale: Adapts when categories are added at runtime; brief's chip names
       become a visual reference, not data
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 7
     Decision: Drop recharts; iPad Reports bar chart uses plain <div>s with
     width: %
     Rationale: Brief's "render with plain divs" wins over PLAN.md's dep list;
       lighter bundle
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 8
     Decision: Frontend converts HEIC → JPEG client-side via heic2any + canvas
       downscale to longest-edge 2048px
     Rationale: iPhone-first; smaller payload; avoids native libheif on Vercel
       functions; no CONTRACTS change
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 9
     Decision: Profile "All time" chip sends from = 1970-01-01T00:00:00.000Z, to
      = 
       now
     Rationale: No CONTRACTS change; backend logic unchanged
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 10
     Decision: Backend agent invents a plausible ~25-category seed across the 4
       programs
     Rationale: No real Jessica email available; aligns with brief sample names
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 11
     Decision: 3 real Clerk users created in dev for the demo
     Rationale: Matches the brief's multi-volunteer History feed

     ---
     Pre-flight CONTRACTS.md amendments (Phase 0 applies these)

     Per CONTRACTS §10's change protocol, the coordinator updates the doc with
     // CHANGED 2026-05-09: notes before agents read it. Five small amendments:

     1. §3 Donation.loggedByName & AuditEvent.actorName clarification — comment:
      "Full name as stored from Clerk; UI is responsible for abbreviating to 
     First L. for display via lib/format-name.ts."
     2. §3 AuditEvent.summary clarification — "Pre-formatted with abbreviated 
     actor name (e.g. Jessica M. logged …). Backend uses the same 
     formatDisplayName helper as frontend."
     3. §4.5 image MIME — note: "iPhone HEIC must be converted to JPEG 
     client-side before posting; backend rejects HEIC."
     4. §4.4 PATCH /api/donations/:id — "If categoryId changes, backend 
     re-snapshots categoryName and programName from the new category. Audit 
     summary names both old and new categories."
     5. §5 add row — All time | from = 1970-01-01T00:00:00Z | to = now.

     ---
     Phase 0 — Coordinator pass (I run after approval)

     Sequential, ~25 min, single push at the end. Tag phase-0-complete.

     1. Move spec docs. git mv CONTRACTS.md PLAN.md wellspring-build-brief.md 
     src/imports/. Update PLAN.md's self-reference (plans/PLAN.md →
     src/imports/PLAN.md) and any frontmatter cross-links.
     2. Apply pre-flight CONTRACTS amendments above.
     3. Scaffold Next.js. npx create-next-app@latest . --ts --app --tailwind 
     --eslint --src-dir --no-import-alias. Verify Tailwind v4 setup (globals.css
      uses @import "tailwindcss").
     4. Install runtime deps. npm i @clerk/nextjs mongoose @google/generative-ai
      zod lucide-react react-hook-form@7.55.0 heic2any. Do not install recharts.
     5. Add src/middleware.ts with Clerk middleware that protects /api/** except
      /api/health.
     6. Add src/lib/types.ts as a verbatim mirror of CONTRACTS.md §3 (with the
     amended comments).
     7. Add src/lib/timezone.ts — export const APP_TZ = "America/Los_Angeles" as
      const;
     8. Add src/lib/format-name.ts with two pure helpers:
       - formatDisplayName(fullName: string): string → "Jessica Martinez" →
     "Jessica M.". Falls back to first word if no last name.
       - getInitials(fullName: string): string → "JM". Falls back to first
     letter if single word.
     9. Add .env.example with CLERK_PUBLISHABLE_KEY, CLERK_SECRET_KEY,
     MONGODB_URI, GOOGLE_API_KEY, NEXT_PUBLIC_APP_URL. Then prompt user to
     populate .env.local.
     10. Initialize Vercel project (vercel link) so both agents push to the same
      preview URL.
     11. Brand color check. Set CSS variables in globals.css: --brand-green: 
     #39900E, --brand-green-dark: #2A6B0A, --brand-green-darkest: #1F4D08,
     --brand-tint: #F7FEE7, --brand-border: #D9F99D, --cta-amber: #F59E0B.
     12. Commit & push in three logical chunks (docs move; scaffold; lib + env).
      Tag final commit.

     ---
     Frontend agent charter

     Owns: src/app/**/* (except src/app/api/**), all *.tsx components, page
     routes, styles, src/app/lib/api-client.ts.

     Reads (does not edit): src/imports/CONTRACTS.md,
     src/imports/wellspring-build-brief.md, src/lib/types.ts,
     src/lib/timezone.ts, src/lib/format-name.ts.

     Must do:
     - Build all 10 screens (9 + the New Category modal) per
     wellspring-build-brief.md §Screens. Mobile + iPad variants for every 
     screen.
     - Implement chrome: BottomTabBar (4 tabs: Log · Reports · History ·
     Profile), TopAppBar (mobile), IpadShell (240 px sidebar + main pane).
     - Build the design-system primitives in
     src/app/components/wellspring/shared.tsx per the brief's §Reusable
     Components list.
     - src/app/lib/api-client.ts — typed wrapper around every CONTRACTS §4
     endpoint. On 401 → window.location.href = "/sign-in". Map ApiError.code →
     toast string via a const ERROR_TOAST_MAP.
     - HEIC pipeline: detect HEIC by MIME or magic bytes → heic2any → canvas
     downscale to longest-edge 2048 px → canvas.toBlob("image/jpeg", 0.85) →
     base64. Cap final ≤ 4 MB.
     - Always derive display name + initials via formatDisplayName / getInitials
      from src/lib/format-name.ts. Never hand-format names anywhere in the UI.
     - All Pacific bucketing (History "Today/Yesterday", Reports preset chips,
     Profile range starts) via Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-US", { timeZone: APP_TZ 
     }). Never use device-local getDate().
     - iPad AI Review must fit 1024 × 768 with overflow: hidden — fix layout,
     don't enable scroll.
     - Strict no-oz rule. Unit is "count" | "lbs" everywhere — copy, dropdowns,
     sample data.
     - Brand color #39900E exact. Do not invent colors.
     - Profile "All time" chip serializes as from = 1970-01-01T00:00:00.000Z, to
      = now.

     Must not:
     - Touch src/app/api/**, src/lib/db/**, src/lib/ai/**, src/lib/auth/**,
     src/lib/seed/**, src/lib/csv.ts, src/lib/audit.ts,
     src/lib/categories-cache.ts.
     - Edit src/lib/types.ts (read-only mirror).
     - Set loggedBy, loggedByName, categoryName, programName, createdAt,
     updatedAt, or deleted on any payload — backend denormalizes.
     - Import recharts. Bars are divs.

     ---
     Backend agent charter

     Owns: src/app/api/**, src/lib/db/**, src/lib/ai/**, src/lib/auth/**,
     src/lib/seed/**, src/lib/csv.ts, src/lib/audit.ts,
     src/lib/categories-cache.ts, and the src/lib/types.ts mirror.

     Reads (does not edit): src/imports/CONTRACTS.md,
     src/imports/wellspring-build-brief.md, src/lib/format-name.ts,
     src/lib/timezone.ts.

     Must do:
     - Mongoose models matching CONTRACTS.md §3 + §8. toJSON transforms project
     _id → id and dates → ISO strings, so wire format == §3 exactly.
     - src/lib/auth/requireAuth.ts: pulls userId from Clerk session, JIT-upserts
      the users doc with name = firstName + " " + lastName (or firstName-only
     fallback), returns { userId, fullName, displayName, initials } where
     displayName/initials come from src/lib/format-name.ts.
     - All denormalization at write time: loggedByName = full name from
     requireAuth, categoryName/programName = lookup of Category doc.
     - src/lib/audit.ts — single recordEvent(type, actor, target, summary)
     helper. Every write route calls it; no inline event inserts. summary uses
     actor.displayName (abbreviated form).
     - Soft-delete only. Donation.deleted = true, Category.active = false.
     List/aggregation endpoints filter deleted: { $ne: true } / active: true.
     - POST /api/donations always accepts an array (Manual Entry sends
     length 1).
     - PATCH /api/donations/:id with categoryId change: re-snapshot categoryName
      + programName from the new category. Audit summary: "qty 12 → 24, category
      Diapers → Adult Diapers".
     - POST /api/recognize: 5 MB cap, base64 with optional data: prefix, 60 s
     in-memory category cache (src/lib/categories-cache.ts), Gemini
     gemini-2.5-flash with dynamic responseSchema populated from active category
      names. Never writes to DB. Cache invalidates on every successful
     POST/PATCH/DELETE /api/categories.
     - GET /api/reports/csv: exact header
     Date,Item,Category,Program,Quantity,Unit,Estimated Value,Source,Logged 
     By,Notes. Pacific dates in filename + Date column. Source column uses human
      labels (AI Photo, Quick Pick, Manual, Barcode).
     - GET /api/reports: implement all three groupBy values (item | category |
     program) even though MVP frontend only sends item — trivial backend cost,
     future-proofs. Tiebreaker on rows: alphabetical itemName ASC.
     - GET /api/profile/me: stats + topCategories (cap 5, "Other" rollup,
     current category names from current categories collection but grouped by
     categoryId snapshot) + recentEntries (last 4 by donatedAt DESC for current
     user, ignoring from/to). Empty range still returns { stats: { entryCount: 
     0, totalValue: 0 }, topCategories: [] }.
     - Concurrent category creation: unique compound index { programId: 1, name:
      1, active: 1 } with collation { locale: "en", strength: 2 }. Catch
     duplicate-key error → 409 CONFLICT.
     - Cross-volunteer edit guard: PATCH/DELETE /api/donations/:id checks
     donation.loggedBy === userId, else 403 FORBIDDEN.
     - Error envelope per CONTRACTS §7 everywhere. No raw stacks. No invented
     error.code values without amending §7 first.
     - Idempotent seed at src/lib/seed/seed.ts (upsert by name): 4 programs, ~25
      categories distributed across them, ~15 catalog items with aliases. Plus
     ~10 historical audit events with synthetic actors Maria T. and Alex K. so
     the History screen looks alive on first load. Run via npm run seed.
     - Manual Entry donatedAt (when frontend sends only a date with no time):
     backend treats it as Pacific 00:00 of that date, converts to UTC ISO,
     stores. (Frontend should send the converted UTC; backend just persists.)

     Must not:
     - Touch src/app/** (except src/app/api/**).
     - Hard-delete anything.
     - Persist photoUrl (always null in MVP).
     - Emit user.created audit events (not in AuditEventType).
     - Serve auth via bearer tokens — only Clerk session cookies.

     ---
     Phase cadence

     PLAN.md §2's four phases stay. Every phase ends with both columns passing
     an integration check before moving on.

     Phase 1 — Foundations. FE: route shells (/sign-in, /log, /log/photo,
     /log/quick, /log/manual, /log/review, /reports, /history, /profile),
     Clerk-wrapped layout, design-system primitives, api-client.ts. BE:
     db/mongoose.ts (cached), models, requireAuth, audit, categories-cache,
     seed, GET /api/health|programs|categories|catalog. ✅ when frontend boots,
     navigates every screen, and Quick Pick / Manual Entry pickers show seeded
     categories + items.

     Phase 2 — Core writes. FE: Manual Entry, Quick Pick (with sticky save bar),
      History feed, Profile chips → aggregations, inline + New category modal.
     BE: POST/PATCH/DELETE /api/donations, POST/PATCH/DELETE /api/categories,
     GET /api/events, GET /api/profile/me. ✅ when end-to-end Manual Entry →
     History → Profile works against live endpoints, including category create
     from inline modal.

     Phase 3 — AI + Reports. FE: Photo Capture → AI Review (HEIC pipeline,
     bail-out toast, + Add item, edited/added/not-in-catalog chips), Reports
     mobile (2 stat cards) + iPad (4 stat cards + table + top-5 div bars), CSV
     export button. BE: POST /api/recognize with Gemini + match-against-catalog,
      GET /api/reports, GET /api/reports/csv. ✅ when the demo storyline works:
     sign in → photo → AI review with ≥3 items → tweak → save → History →
     Reports total updates.

     Phase 4 — Polish. FE: empty states, error toasts wired to ApiError.code
     map, iPad AI Review fits 1024 × 768 with overflow: hidden. BE: tightened
     400 validation messages with field paths, smoke-test seed on a fresh Atlas
     DB.

     ---
     Coordination protocol

     - CONTRACTS.md edits follow CONTRACTS §10: edit first, add // CHANGED 
     2026-05-09: note, ping the other agent, then rely on the new shape. Backend
      regenerates src/lib/types.ts from §3 in the same commit.
     - Shared files (left column of PLAN.md §1 + src/lib/format-name.ts):
     announce in chat → edit → wait for ack.
     - Type drift guard: at the start of each phase, both agents diff
     src/lib/types.ts against CONTRACTS §3 and resolve before continuing.
     - No rebasing the other agent's commits in shared files. If a pull looks
     scrambled, stop and ping.

     │ on a weird file         │ photo, please retake"; user retries (local    │
     │                         │ error, no upload cost)                        │
     ├─────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────┤
     │ Avatar tone is          │ Frontend hashes userId mod 3 → green / amber  │
     │ unspecified in brief    │ / slate; deterministic per user               │
     └─────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────┘

     ---
     Verification (demo acceptance)

     End-to-end checks an unprimed reviewer should pass in one sitting on Vercel
      preview:

     1. Sign in as Jessica on iPhone Safari and iPad Safari.
     2. Take a photo (or upload from gallery, including a HEIC). See ≥ 3 AI
     cards. Edit one quantity → amber Edited chip. Change one category → still
     amber. Add a new category via inline modal → it appears in every dropdown.
     Tap + Add item → green Added chip. Tap Save all → toast → arrive in History
      within 2 s.
     3. Quick Pick — multi-select 3 items → footer shows count + total → save →
     appears in History.
     4. Manual Entry — fill program → category → qty + unit + value + date +
     notes → save → appears in History.
     5. Reports — switch chips (This month → Last month → Q2 → YTD) → totals
     update. iPad shows 4 stat cards + table + top-5 div bars. Click Export CSV
     → file downloads with the exact header row + Pacific filename.
     6. History — Today / Yesterday / older buckets in Pacific. Tap a donation
     event you own → edit/delete sheet. Tap one you don't own → no edit option.
     7. Profile — switch chips including All time. Stats update. Top-5
     categories with Other rollup. iPad shows recent-entries column.
     8. Failure modes — disable network on the phone → take a photo → see AI 
     unavailable — try Quick Pick toast with deep-link button.
     9. 403 path — sign in as Maria, attempt to PATCH a Jessica donation via
     curl → 403 FORBIDDEN with the standard envelope.
     10. No oz anywhere in the rendered UI or CSV — grep the deployed bundle for
      the substring.

❯ How do I get the vercel command                                               

● Two options:

  Easiest — use npx (no install):
  ! npx vercel login
  ! npx vercel link

  Or install globally:
  ! npm i -g vercel
  Then vercel login works directly.

  I'd go with npx for one-off use. The first run downloads the CLI to your npx
  cache and prompts you to confirm — say yes, then it'll proceed to the login
  flow (browser auth or email).

❯ what is it yelling at me for                                                  

● Vercel auto-derived the project name from the directory HackDavis2026 —
  capital letters aren't allowed. Override it with --project:

  ! npx vercel link --yes --project wellspring

  That'll create a Vercel project named wellspring (matches our package.json
  name) and write .vercel/project.json to the repo. Both agents will deploy to
  the same preview URL after that.

❯ whyd it fail to connect lil bro                                               

● Not a blocker — the link itself worked. Linked to 
  subhanmnasirs-projects/springlog (created .vercel) is the line that mattered.
  The Git auto-deploy hookup is what failed, separately.

  Why it failed: Vercel's GitHub App on your account doesn't have permission to
  access SubhanMNasir/HackDavis2026. When you installed the Vercel GitHub App,
  you probably picked "Only select repositories" and this repo wasn't in the
  list (or the app isn't installed at all).

  Two ways to fix (or skip):

  1. Skip it. We don't need GitHub auto-deploy for the demo. We can deploy
  manually with npx vercel (preview) or npx vercel --prod from the CLI. That's
  actually how the build brief implies we'll be deploying anyway.
  2. Fix it later. Go to https://github.com/apps/vercel/installations/new →
  grant access to HackDavis2026. After that, future commits auto-deploy. You can
   do this anytime from the Vercel dashboard → Settings → Git.

  Since we're done with Phase 0 setup, let me verify .vercel/project.json got
  written and then commit + tag. Then we can spawn the agents.

● Yes, http://localhost:3000 is correct for local dev — that's what next dev
  defaults to (and matches .env.example).

  A few notes:

  - NEXT_PUBLIC_APP_URL is mostly nice-to-have here. Frontend api-client.ts
  calls relative paths (/api/donations), so it doesn't actually need an absolute
   base URL. It's mainly useful if Clerk redirects need an absolute URL or if
  anything generates emails/share links with a full URL.
  - Vercel preview/prod: don't put those URLs in your local .env. Vercel injects
   VERCEL_URL automatically per-deploy. For preview/prod you'd set
  NEXT_PUBLIC_APP_URL in the Vercel dashboard → Settings → Environment
  Variables, scoped to the right environment.
  - If you want to skip it: you could just leave the var unset locally and the
  frontend would still work, since nothing in the MVP critically depends on it.
  But setting http://localhost:3000 is the safe default and matches the example.

  So for .env: NEXT_PUBLIC_APP_URL=http://localhost:3000 is the right call.

  The two real blockers are still MONGODB_URI (Atlas M10 connection string) and
  GOOGLE_API_KEY (Gemini). Once those are in, we're cleared to spawn.

     ~/.claude/plans/hi-claude-utilize-contracts-md-magical-backus.md · /plan to
      edit
     Wellspring — Two-Agent Rollout Plan

     Context

     Wellspring Women's Center needs an MVP donation logger to replace a paper
     log: mobile-first volunteer app, iPad variant for every screen, Clerk auth,
      MongoDB persistence, Gemini photo recognition, soft-deletes + audit log on
      every write. Three spec docs already exist at the repo root:

     - CONTRACTS.md — wire-format middleware between agents
     - PLAN.md — phasing & file ownership
     - wellspring-build-brief.md — visual + screen spec

     Current repo state: docs only. Zero scaffolding — no src/, no package.json,
      no .env*, no .claude/. The references in PLAN.md to "the existing static
     mockup at src/app/App.tsx" and "shadcn/ui already available in
     src/app/components/ui/" do not exist; Phase 1 frontend builds routes from
     the brief's screen specs from scratch (the brief is detailed enough to do
     that).

     Goal: kick off a frontend agent and a backend agent that build in parallel,
      each treating CONTRACTS.md as the contract of record. Demo target: Vercel
     preview deploy.

     ---
     Decisions locked in this session

     #: 1
     Decision: I run Phase 0 as a single coordinator pass after plan approval
     Rationale: Atomic seed; both agents fork off cleanly with no race on shared

       scaffolding
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 2
     Decision: MongoDB Atlas M10 cluster (user-provisioned)
     Rationale: Production-grade tier, dedicated resources
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 3
     Decision: Clerk + Mongo Atlas + Gemini all live from day 1
     Rationale: No service stubs; agents wire real services from Phase 1
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 4
     Decision: All three spec docs move to src/imports/
     Rationale: Co-locates docs with code; matches the layout PLAN.md §1 already

       implies
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 5
     Decision: loggedByName / actorName stored as full name (Jessica Martinez);
     UI
       renders abbreviated (Jessica M.) via a shared helper
     Rationale: Single canonical record in DB, flexible display
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 6
     Decision: Quick Pick chips populate dynamically from /api/categories
     Rationale: Adapts when categories are added at runtime; brief's chip names
       become a visual reference, not data
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 7
     Decision: Drop recharts; iPad Reports bar chart uses plain <div>s with
     width: %
     Rationale: Brief's "render with plain divs" wins over PLAN.md's dep list;
       lighter bundle
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 8
     Decision: Frontend converts HEIC → JPEG client-side via heic2any + canvas
       downscale to longest-edge 2048px
     Rationale: iPhone-first; smaller payload; avoids native libheif on Vercel
       functions; no CONTRACTS change
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 9
     Decision: Profile "All time" chip sends from = 1970-01-01T00:00:00.000Z, to
      = 
       now
     Rationale: No CONTRACTS change; backend logic unchanged
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     #: 10
     Decision: Backend agent invents a plausible ~25-category seed across the 4
       programs
     Rationale: No real Jessica email available; aligns with brief sample names

     ---
     Frontend agent charter

     Owns: src/app/**/* (except src/app/api/**), all *.tsx components, page
     routes, styles, src/app/lib/api-client.ts.

     Reads (does not edit): src/imports/CONTRACTS.md,
     src/imports/wellspring-build-brief.md, src/lib/types.ts,
     src/lib/timezone.ts, src/lib/format-name.ts.

     Must do:
     - Build all 10 screens (9 + the New Category modal) per
     wellspring-build-brief.md §Screens. Mobile + iPad variants for every 
     screen.
     - Implement chrome: BottomTabBar (4 tabs: Log · Reports · History ·
     Profile), TopAppBar (mobile), IpadShell (240 px sidebar + main pane).
     - Build the design-system primitives in
     src/app/components/wellspring/shared.tsx per the brief's §Reusable
     Components list.
     - src/app/lib/api-client.ts — typed wrapper around every CONTRACTS §4
     endpoint. On 401 → window.location.href = "/sign-in". Map ApiError.code →
     toast string via a const ERROR_TOAST_MAP.
     - HEIC pipeline: detect HEIC by MIME or magic bytes → heic2any → canvas
     downscale to longest-edge 2048 px → canvas.toBlob("image/jpeg", 0.85) →
     base64. Cap final ≤ 4 MB.
     - Always derive display name + initials via formatDisplayName / getInitials
      from src/lib/format-name.ts. Never hand-format names anywhere in the UI.
     - All Pacific bucketing (History "Today/Yesterday", Reports preset chips,
     Profile range starts) via Intl.DateTimeFormat("en-US", { timeZone: APP_TZ 
     }). Never use device-local getDate().
     - iPad AI Review must fit 1024 × 768 with overflow: hidden — fix layout,
     don't enable scroll.
     - Strict no-oz rule. Unit is "count" | "lbs" everywhere — copy, dropdowns,
     sample data.
     - Brand color #39900E exact. Do not invent colors.
     - Profile "All time" chip serializes as from = 1970-01-01T00:00:00.000Z, to
      = now.

     Must not:
     - Touch src/app/api/**, src/lib/db/**, src/lib/ai/**, src/lib/auth/**,
     src/lib/seed/**, src/lib/csv.ts, src/lib/audit.ts,
     src/lib/categories-cache.ts.
     - Edit src/lib/types.ts (read-only mirror).
     - Set loggedBy, loggedByName, categoryName, programName, createdAt,
     updatedAt, or deleted on any payload — backend denormalizes.
     - Import recharts. Bars are divs.

     ---
     Backend agent charter

     Owns: src/app/api/**, src/lib/db/**, src/lib/ai/**, src/lib/auth/**,
     src/lib/seed/**, src/lib/csv.ts, src/lib/audit.ts,
     src/lib/categories-cache.ts, and the src/lib/types.ts mirror.

     Reads (does not edit): src/imports/CONTRACTS.md,
     src/imports/wellspring-build-brief.md, src/lib/format-name.ts,
     src/lib/timezone.ts.

     Must do:
     - Mongoose models matching CONTRACTS.md §3 + §8. toJSON transforms project
     _id → id and dates → ISO strings, so wire format == §3 exactly.
     - src/lib/auth/requireAuth.ts: pulls userId from Clerk session, JIT-upserts
      the users doc with name = firstName + " " + lastName (or firstName-only
     fallback), returns { userId, fullName, displayName, initials } where
     displayName/initials come from src/lib/format-name.ts.
     - All denormalization at write time: loggedByName = full name from
     requireAuth, categoryName/programName = lookup of Category doc.
     - src/lib/audit.ts — single recordEvent(type, actor, target, summary)
     helper. Every write route calls it; no inline event inserts. summary uses
     actor.displayName (abbreviated form).
     - Soft-delete only. Donation.deleted = true, Category.active = false.
     List/aggregation endpoints filter deleted: { $ne: true } / active: true.
     - POST /api/donations always accepts an array (Manual Entry sends
     length 1).
     - PATCH /api/donations/:id with categoryId change: re-snapshot categoryName
      + programName from the new category. Audit summary: "qty 12 → 24, category
      Diapers → Adult Diapers".
     - POST /api/recognize: 5 MB cap, base64 with optional data: prefix, 60 s
     in-memory category cache (src/lib/categories-cache.ts), Gemini
     gemini-2.5-flash with dynamic responseSchema populated from active category
      names. Never writes to DB. Cache invalidates on every successful
     POST/PATCH/DELETE /api/categories.
     - GET /api/reports/csv: exact header
     Date,Item,Category,Program,Quantity,Unit,Estimated Value,Source,Logged 
     By,Notes. Pacific dates in filename + Date column. Source column uses human
      labels (AI Photo, Quick Pick, Manual, Barcode).
     - GET /api/reports: implement all three groupBy values (item | category |
     program) even though MVP frontend only sends item — trivial backend cost,
     future-proofs. Tiebreaker on rows: alphabetical itemName ASC.
     - GET /api/profile/me: stats + topCategories (cap 5, "Other" rollup,
     current category names from current categories collection but grouped by
     categoryId snapshot) + recentEntries (last 4 by donatedAt DESC for current
     user, ignoring from/to). Empty range still returns { stats: { entryCount: 
     0, totalValue: 0 }, topCategories: [] }.
     - Concurrent category creation: unique compound index { programId: 1, name:
      1, active: 1 } with collation { locale: "en", strength: 2 }. Catch
     duplicate-key error → 409 CONFLICT.
     - Cross-volunteer edit guard: PATCH/DELETE /api/donations/:id checks
     donation.loggedBy === userId, else 403 FORBIDDEN.
     - Error envelope per CONTRACTS §7 everywhere. No raw stacks. No invented
     error.code values without amending §7 first.
     - Idempotent seed at src/lib/seed/seed.ts (upsert by name): 4 programs, ~25
      categories distributed across them, ~15 catalog items with aliases. Plus
     ~10 historical audit events with synthetic actors Maria T. and Alex K. so
     the History screen looks alive on first load. Run via npm run seed.
     - Manual Entry donatedAt (when frontend sends only a date with no time):
     backend treats it as Pacific 00:00 of that date, converts to UTC ISO,
     stores. (Frontend should send the converted UTC; backend just persists.)

     Must not:
     - Touch src/app/** (except src/app/api/**).
     - Hard-delete anything.
     - Persist photoUrl (always null in MVP).
     - Emit user.created audit events (not in AuditEventType).
     - Serve auth via bearer tokens — only Clerk session cookies.

     ---
     Phase cadence

     PLAN.md §2's four phases stay. Every phase ends with both columns passing
     an integration check before moving on.

     Phase 1 — Foundations. FE: route shells (/sign-in, /log, /log/photo,
     /log/quick, /log/manual, /log/review, /reports, /history, /profile),
     Clerk-wrapped layout, design-system primitives, api-client.ts. BE:
     db/mongoose.ts (cached), models, requireAuth, audit, categories-cache,
     seed, GET /api/health|programs|categories|catalog. ✅ when frontend boots,
     navigates every screen, and Quick Pick / Manual Entry pickers show seeded
     categories + items.

     Phase 2 — Core writes. FE: Manual Entry, Quick Pick (with sticky save bar),
      History feed, Profile chips → aggregations, inline + New category modal.
     BE: POST/PATCH/DELETE /api/donations, POST/PATCH/DELETE /api/categories,
     GET /api/events, GET /api/profile/me. ✅ when end-to-end Manual Entry →
     History → Profile works against live endpoints, including category create
     from inline modal.

     Phase 3 — AI + Reports. FE: Photo Capture → AI Review (HEIC pipeline,
     bail-out toast, + Add item, edited/added/not-in-catalog chips), Reports
     mobile (2 stat cards) + iPad (4 stat cards + table + top-5 div bars), CSV
     export button. BE: POST /api/recognize with Gemini + match-against-catalog,
      GET /api/reports, GET /api/reports/csv. ✅ when the demo storyline works:
     sign in → photo → AI review with ≥3 items → tweak → save → History →
     Reports total updates.

     Phase 4 — Polish. FE: empty states, error toasts wired to ApiError.code
     map, iPad AI Review fits 1024 × 768 with overflow: hidden. BE: tightened
     400 validation messages with field paths, smoke-test seed on a fresh Atlas
     DB.

     ---
     Coordination protocol

     - CONTRACTS.md edits follow CONTRACTS §10: edit first, add // CHANGED 
     2026-05-09: note, ping the other agent, then rely on the new shape. Backend
      regenerates src/lib/types.ts from §3 in the same commit.
     - Shared files (left column of PLAN.md §1 + src/lib/format-name.ts):
     announce in chat → edit → wait for ack.
     - Type drift guard: at the start of each phase, both agents diff
     src/lib/types.ts against CONTRACTS §3 and resolve before continuing.
     - No rebasing the other agent's commits in shared files. If a pull looks
     scrambled, stop and ping.

     ---
     Verification (demo acceptance)

     End-to-end checks an unprimed reviewer should pass in one sitting on Vercel
      preview:

     1. Sign in as Jessica on iPhone Safari and iPad Safari.
     2. Take a photo (or upload from gallery, including a HEIC). See ≥ 3 AI
     cards. Edit one quantity → amber Edited chip. Change one category → still
     amber. Add a new category via inline modal → it appears in every dropdown.
     Tap + Add item → green Added chip. Tap Save all → toast → arrive in History
      within 2 s.
     3. Quick Pick — multi-select 3 items → footer shows count + total → save →
     appears in History.
     4. Manual Entry — fill program → category → qty + unit + value + date +
     notes → save → appears in History.
     5. Reports — switch chips (This month → Last month → Q2 → YTD) → totals
     update. iPad shows 4 stat cards + table + top-5 div bars. Click Export CSV
     → file downloads with the exact header row + Pacific filename.
     6. History — Today / Yesterday / older buckets in Pacific. Tap a donation
     event you own → edit/delete sheet. Tap one you don't own → no edit option.
     7. Profile — switch chips including All time. Stats update. Top-5
     categories with Other rollup. iPad shows recent-entries column.
     8. Failure modes — disable network on the phone → take a photo → see AI 
     unavailable — try Quick Pick toast with deep-link button.
     9. 403 path — sign in as Maria, attempt to PATCH a Jessica donation via
     curl → 403 FORBIDDEN with the standard envelope.
     10. No oz anywhere in the rendered UI or CSV — grep the deployed bundle for
      the substring.

     Fix Tailwind v4 oxide native-binding error

     Context

     npm run build (Turbopack) is failing on ./src/app/globals.css with:

     Error: Cannot find module '@tailwindcss/oxide-linux-x64-gnu'
     Require stack:
     - node_modules/@tailwindcss/oxide/index.js
     - node_modules/@tailwindcss/postcss/dist/index.js

     Root cause: Tailwind v4's CSS engine is compiled Rust (oxide) and ships
     native bindings as optional, platform-specific sub-packages
     (@tailwindcss/oxide-linux-x64-gnu, @tailwindcss/oxide-darwin-arm64, etc.).
     The wrapper at @tailwindcss/oxide/index.js require()s the binding for the
     current platform.

     npm 9 has a known bug (npm/cli#4828
     (https://github.com/npm/cli/issues/4828)) where optionalDependencies
     resolved in the lockfile are not always materialized into node_modules on
     install — most often when the lockfile was generated on a different
     platform or a prior install ran with --ignore-optional/--omit=optional.

     Confirmed in this repo (just inspected):
     - node_modules/@tailwindcss/oxide/ ✅ present (JS wrapper)
     - node_modules/@tailwindcss/oxide-linux-x64-gnu/ ❌ missing (the actual
     .node binary)
     - package-lock.json references oxide-linux 15 times ✅ — npm knows about 
     it, just didn't install it
     - No .npmrc excluding optional deps
     - Platform: WSL2 Linux x86_64 (matches the linux-x64-gnu triple expected)

     The error message itself prescribes the canonical fix: wipe and reinstall.

     Recommended fix — clean reinstall

     This is what npm tells you to do in the error and is the only fix that
     produces a consistent, reproducible lockfile for teammates / Vercel:

     rm -rf node_modules package-lock.json
     npm install

     Why this is the right call:
     - Regenerates package-lock.json with the optional binding properly resolved
      for this platform.
     - Vercel build runs on Linux x64 (same triple), so the regenerated lockfile
      produces identical builds locally and on Vercel.
     - Reinstall is ~2 min — short enough to not matter for the demo.
     - Avoids any band-aid that future agents/teammates would have to re-apply
     on every fresh checkout.

     Watch-out: Re-running npm install may bump some transitive deps (anything
     with a ^ range). Spot-check git diff --stat package-lock.json after — if
     anything material moved (Clerk, Mongoose, Next.js minor), eyeball it;
     otherwise commit the new lockfile alongside the fix.

     Quick band-aid fallback (only if the clean reinstall is unacceptable)

     If you need the build working right now and don't want to touch the
     lockfile:

     npm i @tailwindcss/oxide-linux-x64-gnu --no-save

     Drops the missing binary into node_modules/ without modifying package.json
     or package-lock.json. Build will work. But anyone who runs npm install
     again (Vercel CI, a teammate, you tomorrow after rm -rf node_modules) will
     hit the same error. This is what the Phase 1 agent worktrees did because
     they were ephemeral. For main, do the clean reinstall.

     Verification

     After the reinstall, verify in this order:

     1. Native binding present:
     ls node_modules/@tailwindcss/oxide-linux-x64-gnu/tailwindcss-oxide.linux-x6
     4-gnu.node
     1. Should print the path, not No such file or directory.
     2. Lockfile resolves the binding:
     grep -A1 '"node_modules/@tailwindcss/oxide-linux-x64-gnu"'
     package-lock.json | head
     2. Should show a "resolved": "https://registry.npmjs.org/..." line.
     3. Build passes:
     npm run build
     3. Should complete without the native-binding error and emit a normal
     Next.js production-build summary.
     4. Dev server still boots (kill the running background bkzp5of04 first — it
      has stale node_modules in memory):
     npm run dev
     # then: curl -s http://localhost:3000/api/health
     4. Should return {"ok":true,...} and /api/programs should still 401 with
     the §7 envelope.
     5. Sanity-check the lockfile diff (informational):
     git diff --stat package-lock.json
     5. Large diff (>500 lines beyond the oxide entries) → eyeball top-level dep
      moves. Small diff → just commit.

     Files affected

     - package-lock.json — regenerated. Stage + commit once build passes.
     - node_modules/ — wiped and regenerated. Not in git (.gitignore line 4).
     - No source files touched. Pure dependency-resolution fix; nothing in src/
     changes.

     Commit (after verification)

     Single commit on main, no trailer:

     fix(deps): regenerate lockfile to materialize @tailwindcss/oxide native
     binding

     npm 9 optional-deps bug (#4828) silently skipped
     @tailwindcss/oxide-linux-x64-gnu
     on the prior install, breaking `npm run build` with "Cannot find native
     binding".
     Wiping node_modules + package-lock.json and reinstalling pulls the
     platform-specific
     binary in correctly. No source changes; only package-lock.json moves.

     Out of scope

     - Upgrading Node 18 → 20 (Tailwind v4 emitted Node-20 warnings during
     scaffold; not the cause of this error).
     - Switching from npm → pnpm/bun (would dodge the bug entirely but diverges
     from Vercel's default install). Defer.
     - Pinning @tailwindcss/postcss to a specific minor — the ^4 range is fine;
     the bug is in npm, not Tailwind.

● Fix is shipped. Summary:

  What was wrong: Tailwind v4's @tailwindcss/oxide native binding requires Node
  ≥ 20 per its engines field. We were on Node 18.19.1, so npm correctly skipped
  the optional @tailwindcss/oxide-linux-x64-gnu package, and the build crashed

  What I did (proper fix):

  5. npm run build → all 18 routes built clean, no native-binding error

  → 200 {ok:true,...}

  What changed in git:
  - package-lock.json — 3-line diff. Only react-hook-form minor-bumped 7.55.0 →
  7.75.0 (allowed by the ^7.55.0 range; 7.x is API-stable, no breaking changes).
  - ~/.bashrc got nvm sourcing appended (outside the repo, not tracked).
  - No source files touched.

  Caveats:
  - The shell snapshot Bash uses doesn't auto-source nvm, so future tool calls
  in this session need . ~/.nvm/nvm.sh && nvm use --lts && ... prefix. I'll
  handle that.
  - New terminal windows you open will pick up Node 24 from ~/.bashrc
  automatically.
  - Vercel build will be unaffected — Vercel uses its own Node 24 LTS default.

  Dev server is live at http://localhost:3000 — ready when you want to
  browser-test. Let me know if you want me to commit the lockfile bump.

     Fix Clerk "Secret Key is invalid" handshake error

     Context

     Clerk middleware is throwing at runtime:

     Clerk: Handshake token verification failed: The provided Clerk Secret Key
     is invalid.
     Make sure that your Clerk Secret Key is correct.
     (reason=secret-key-invalid, token-carrier=undefined)

     Variable names are correct. I just inspected .env — both keys are present
     under the canonical names that @clerk/nextjs ^7.3.3 reads automatically:

     ┌───────────────────────────────────┬──────────┬────────┬──────────────────
     ┐
     │                Var                │  Prefix  │ Length │      Status
     │
     ├───────────────────────────────────┼──────────┼────────┼──────────────────
     ┤
     │                                   │          │        │ borderline-short
     │
     │ NEXT_PUBLIC_CLERK_PUBLISHABLE_KEY │ pk_test_ │ 55     │  for current
     │
     │                                   │          │ chars  │ Clerk format
     │
     │                                   │          │        │ (typical: 60+)
     │
     ├───────────────────────────────────┼──────────┼────────┼──────────────────
     ┤
     │                                   │          │        │ likely truncated
     │
     │ CLERK_SECRET_KEY                  │ sk_test_ │ 51     │  — current Clerk
     │
     │                                   │          │ chars  │  secret keys are
     │
     │                                   │          │        │  ~60-72 chars
     │
     └───────────────────────────────────┴──────────┴────────┴──────────────────
     ┘

     The naming is fine. The Clerk Next.js SDK reads exactly these two variable
     names automatically — you do not need any other names like CLERK_API_KEY,
     CLERK_FRONTEND_API, CLERK_PUBLIC_KEY, etc. Those are old/deprecated.

     So the fix isn't about renaming. The secret key value itself is being
     rejected by Clerk's API as invalid. There are exactly three things this
     typically means:

     1. The secret key got truncated on copy-paste (most likely — 51 chars is
     short)
     2. The publishable key and secret key are from different Clerk applications
      (e.g., copied pk from one app, sk from another — the publishable key tells
      Clerk which instance to validate against, then the secret has to match
     that instance)
     3. The Clerk app was deleted or the API keys were rotated, so the old key
     no longer exists in Clerk's database

     What "title" / variable names you need

     These are the only two names that matter for sign-in to work. Both already
     correctly named in your .env:

     # Public — exposed to the browser. Must start with pk_test_ or pk_live_.
     NEXT_PUBLIC_CLERK_PUBLISHABLE_KEY=pk_test_...

     # Server-only secret. Must start with sk_test_ or sk_live_.
     # Never prefix with NEXT_PUBLIC_ or it'll leak to the browser bundle.
     CLERK_SECRET_KEY=sk_test_...

     @clerk/nextjs reads them via process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_CLERK_PUBLISHABLE_KEY
     and process.env.CLERK_SECRET_KEY — no other configuration plumbing needed.

     What value to paste

     Get fresh keys from Clerk and copy from the same app:

     1. Go to https://dashboard.clerk.com
     2. Top-left dropdown → confirm you're in the Wellspring / Springlog app (or
      whatever you named it). If multiple apps exist, pick the one you want this
      dev environment pointed at.
     3. Sidebar → API keys (under Developers).
     4. Under Quick Copy, you should see the .env snippet. Click the copy icon
     next to both lines. They're guaranteed to be from the same app and not
     truncated.
     5. Open .env, replace the existing two lines with the freshly-copied pair.
     6. Save.
     7. Restart npm run dev — Next.js does NOT hot-reload env changes; the
     running dev server (bkxitr95n in the background) is still using the cached
     invalid key.

     If you only see a "show" toggle (no Quick-Copy block), that's fine — just
     toggle "show" on each key and copy each value individually, paste into .env
      as NEXT_PUBLIC_CLERK_PUBLISHABLE_KEY=... and CLERK_SECRET_KEY=.... Don't 
     wrap the values in quotes — Next.js handles this fine, but quotes can
     occasionally cause surprises with special characters.

     Sanity-check after pasting (without exposing the value)

     I can run a small awk script that prints only var names + first 8 chars +
     length, the same one I ran during diagnosis. Expect to see:

     NEXT_PUBLIC_CLERK_PUBLISHABLE_KEY = pk_test_... (len ≥ 60)
     CLERK_SECRET_KEY                  = sk_test_... (len ≥ 60)

     If CLERK_SECRET_KEY is still 51 chars after paste, the copy got cut again —
      try copying with the explicit copy icon rather than triple-click
     highlighting.

     What I won't change

     - No source code edits. src/middleware.ts and the Clerk SDK are wired
     correctly; the bug is purely in the .env value.
     - No new env vars. Resist any temptation to add CLERK_API_KEY,
     CLERK_PEM_PUBLIC_KEY, CLERK_JWT_KEY, etc. — the SDK doesn't need them for
     handshake verification in this setup.
     - No .env.local. Adding a second env file just creates load-order
     surprises. Keep everything in the single .env.

     Files affected

     - .env — two lines updated by the user (or by me if user pastes the values
     into chat).
     - No git changes. .env is in .gitignore (line 34) and stays untracked. The
     committed .env.example already documents both var names correctly.

     Verification

     1. After pasting fresh keys + restarting dev:
     . ~/.nvm/nvm.sh && nvm use --lts >/dev/null && npm run dev
     1. (The nvm prefix is needed because the shell snapshot doesn't auto-source
      nvm — same as we discovered during the Tailwind fix.)
     2. Public route still works:
     curl -s http://localhost:3000/api/health
     # → {"ok":true,"time":"..."}
     2. (This worked even with the broken key because /api/health is in the
     isPublicRoute matcher in src/middleware.ts:4-8.)
     3. Protected route returns the right envelope:
     curl -si http://localhost:3000/api/programs | head -5
     # → HTTP/1.1 401
     # → {"error":{"code":"UNAUTHENTICATED","message":"Authentication 
     required"}}
     3. With a valid secret, this should still 401 (no session) but not crash
     with the handshake error in the dev server logs. If you tail the dev log
     and don't see Handshake token verification failed, the secret is now
     accepted by Clerk.
     4. Browser sign-in flow:
       - Open http://localhost:3000 in a browser
       - Should redirect to /sign-in
       - Clerk's hosted sign-in widget should render (logo, email field). If it
     errors with "Application not found" or similar, the publishable key is from
      a different/deleted app — check Clerk dashboard again.
       - Sign in with a test user
       - Should land on /log with the three method cards rendered
     5. JIT user upsert smoke test (after you sign in once):
     In MongoDB Atlas, the users collection in your Wellspring DB should have
     one new doc with clerkId matching your Clerk user ID, populated by
     src/lib/auth/requireAuth.ts on the first authed request.

     If a fresh paste from the dashboard still fails

     In order of likelihood:

     1. The Clerk app was deleted/recreated. Confirm the app exists in the
     dashboard.
     2. You're on the wrong instance. Clerk apps have separate Development and
     Production instances; sk_test_ is dev, sk_live_ is prod. Mixing dev
     publishable + prod secret (or vice versa) fails handshake. Both should be
     _test_ for now.
     3. Trailing whitespace / newline in .env. Some terminal pastes append a
     CR/LF. The awk sanity check would show the length is 1 char too long. Fix:
     open .env in an editor, ensure each line ends cleanly with no trailing
     spaces.
     4. Special characters not escaped. Clerk keys are URL-safe base64 — no
     special chars — so this is unlikely, but if you ever see $, \, or backticks
      in a secret, wrap in single quotes.

     If after a fresh paste the error persists with the dev server restarted,
     paste the new lengths from the sanity check (not the values themselves) and
      I'll dig further.

     Out of scope

     - Setting up Clerk webhooks → Mongo (PLAN.md out of scope — JIT upsert is
     the chosen pattern).
     - Production Clerk instance / sk_live_ keys (we're targeting Vercel
     preview, not production-prod).
     - Custom Clerk sign-in UI (/sign-in/[[...sign-in]]) — current app uses
     Clerk's hosted widget.

     ~/.claude/plans/hi-claude-utilize-contracts-md-magical-backus.md · /plan to

     Phase 2 — Wire write endpoints + interactive screens

     Context

     Phase 1 shipped (read endpoints, route shells, design system, Clerk auth,
     seed). Sign-in just verified working end-to-end. The user wants to know:

     1. Will the UI be more functional? — short answer: yes, this is exactly
     Phase 2's scope.
     2. Will the database feel faster? — short answer: mostly yes, but with a 
     distinction.

     User flagged two specific slow moments:

     - First hit per route (3-5s) — this is Turbopack compile-on-demand in dev 
     mode. It is not a database problem. Next.js dev compiles each route the
     first time you navigate to it. In production / Vercel preview, every route 
     is pre-built at deploy time, so this lag disappears entirely. Phase 2
     doesn't change this in dev (it's a Next.js architecture choice), but the
     deployed app the demo will run against will not have it.
     - Data loading after sign-in — this is a mix of (a) the same Turbopack lag
     for /api/categories|catalog|programs first-hit, plus (b) Mongoose
     cold-connection on the first DB-touching request (~500-1500ms to handshake
     with Atlas). After that first request, the cached connection makes
     subsequent queries ~50-150ms. Phase 2 does improve perceived speed here —
     see "Performance" below.

     So: Phase 2's main job is to wire the interactive screens to real write
     endpoints. There's also a small, targeted set of perf wins we can include
     without bloating scope.

     Current state (just inspected)

     Backend routes implemented (4 of ~13):
     - GET /api/health, GET /api/programs, GET /api/categories, GET /api/catalog

     Backend routes missing (all of these are Phase 2 work):
     - POST /api/donations (bulk insert + denormalize + audit event)
     - PATCH /api/donations/:id, DELETE /api/donations/:id (with cross-volunteer
      403, soft-delete, re-snapshot on category change)
     - POST /api/categories (with 409 CONFLICT on case-insensitive duplicate)
     - PATCH /api/categories/:id, DELETE /api/categories/:id
     - GET /api/events (audit feed with from/to/actor/type filters)
     - GET /api/profile/me (per CONTRACTS §4.9)

     (Phase 3 adds /api/recognize, /api/reports, /api/reports/csv. Out of scope
     here.)

     Frontend screens scaffolded but not wired:
     - log/manual/page.tsx — 233 lines, has form state but no submit-to-API
     - log/quick/page.tsx — 180 lines, has multi-select state but no save
     - history/page.tsx — 56 lines, pure shell
     - profile/page.tsx — 113 lines, has range-chip UI but no fetch

     Phase 2 scope

     Backend agent work (src/app/api/**, src/lib/** writes)

     1. POST /api/donations — accepts an array (length 1 or N). For each: lookup
      category → snapshot categoryName + programName; pull actor's full name
     from requireAuth; insert; emit donation.created audit events with summary
     "Jessica M. logged 12 lbs Diapers (Diapers Pantry)" (per CONTRACTS §3 +
     format-name helper).
     2. PATCH /api/donations/:id — cross-volunteer guard (donation.loggedBy === 
     userId else 403). On categoryId change, re-snapshot categoryName +
     programName. Audit summary names old → new fields.
     3. DELETE /api/donations/:id — soft-delete (deleted: true); same
     cross-volunteer guard; emit donation.deleted event.
     4. POST /api/categories — validate programId, insert, catch dup-key error
     from the case-insensitive compound index → return 409 CONFLICT. Invalidate
     categories-cache on success.
     5. PATCH /api/categories/:id — rename only (no program re-parent). Emit
     category.renamed with "old → new". Invalidate cache.
     6. DELETE /api/categories/:id — soft-delete (active: false). Invalidate
     cache. (Donations referencing it stay valid via the snapshot fields.)
     7. GET /api/events — read audit log with from, to, actor, type filters
     (default limit 50, sort createdAt DESC).
     8. GET /api/profile/me?from&to — stats (entryCount, totalValue),
     topCategories (cap 5, group by categoryId with current name lookup, "Other"
      rollup), recentEntries (last 4 by donatedAt DESC ignoring range — per
     CONTRACTS §4.9).

     Frontend agent work (src/app/(app)/**, src/app/components/**)

     1. Manual Entry — wire the existing form's submit to
     apiClient.createDonations([single]) → success toast → router push to
     /history. Convert selected date to UTC ISO of Pacific 00:00 before send.
     2. Quick Pick — wire multi-select state to a sticky save bar showing count
     + dollar total; on save, batch POST. Empty selection → bar hidden.
     3. Inline + New category modal — present from Quick Pick & Manual Entry &
     AI Review (Phase 3). On 409, show "Category already exists in this program"
      inline. On success, refetch categories so all dropdowns refresh.
     4. History feed — fetch /api/events, bucket by Pacific date (Today /
     Yesterday / older MMM D), render rows from each event's summary field. Tap
     own donation → edit/delete sheet. Mobile + iPad layouts.
     5. Profile — wire range chips (Today, This week, This month, This year, All
      time, Custom) to /api/profile/me. iPad shows recent-entries column.
     6. Toast wiring — every apiClient ApiError.code mapped via existing
     error-toast-map.ts.

     Performance — what actually changes

     ┌──────────────┬───────────────────┬───────────────────┬──────────────────┐
     │    Where     │      Before       │  After Phase 2    │  After Vercel    │
     │              │                   │       (dev)       │     preview      │
     ├──────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼──────────────────┤
     │ Dev server   │ 22s               │ 22s (no change —  │ n/a (no dev      │
     │ boot         │                   │ Turbopack)        │ server)          │
     ├──────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼──────────────────┤
     │ First hit    │ 3-5s compile      │ 3-5s compile (no  │ <100ms —         │
     │ per route    │                   │ change in dev)    │ pre-built        │
     ├──────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼──────────────────┤
     │ First DB     │ 500-1500ms cold   │ ~200-400ms if we  │ ~50-150ms (Fluid │
     │ query        │ connection +      │ prefetch (see     │  Compute warm    │
     │              │ compile           │ below)            │ reuse)           │
     ├──────────────┼───────────────────┼───────────────────┼──────────────────┤
     │ Subsequent   │ 50-150ms          │ 50-150ms          │ 50-150ms         │
     │ queries      │                   │                   │                  │
     └──────────────┴───────────────────┴───────────────────┴──────────────────┘

     The targeted dev-mode perf win we'll include (no extra scope, fits
     naturally inside Phase 2):

     - Prefetch in (app)/layout.tsx: kick off apiClient.getPrograms() and
     apiClient.getCategories() as soon as the layout mounts (parallel,
     fire-and-forget into a small in-memory cache on the api-client). By the
     time the user navigates to /log/manual or /log/quick, the data is already
     there. Side benefit: warms the Mongoose connection too.
     - Single round-trip dropdowns: /log/manual already needs programs +
     categories + catalog. Phase 2 ensures the api-client kicks all three in
     parallel via Promise.all, not sequentially.

     Both of these collapse the "data loading after sign-in" experience to one
     short stall (during the first Turbopack compile of
     /api/programs|categories|catalog) instead of three sequential ones.

     The bigger perf story is that Vercel preview won't have the Turbopack lag 
     at all — that's the demo target, and it'll be snappy. The dev-server
     slowness is a development-time artifact you'll feel only while building,
     not while demoing.

     Phase 2 does not include

     - Photo capture / AI Review / POST /api/recognize → Phase 3
     - Reports (mobile + iPad) / GET /api/reports / CSV export → Phase 3
     - Empty-state polish, 1024×768 iPad-AI-Review fit → Phase 4

     Execution model

     Per the existing rollout plan: two agents in parallel with isolated git
     worktrees.

     - BE agent owns src/app/api/** + src/lib/{audit,categories-cache,db}/**
     writes. Cannot touch src/app/(app|auth)/**.
     - FE agent owns src/app/(app)/** + src/app/components/** +
     src/app/lib/api-client.ts. Cannot touch src/app/api/** or
     src/lib/{db,auth,audit,seed}/**.
     - Both treat src/imports/CONTRACTS.md as wire-format law.
     - Coordinator (me) merges both with --no-ff, runs the integration check
     (tsc, sign-in → save donation → see in History → see in Profile
     aggregations), tags phase-2-complete, pushes.

     Estimated wall-clock: ~30-40 minutes per agent in parallel.

     Critical files to be modified or created

     Backend (created by BE agent):
     - src/app/api/donations/route.ts (POST)
     - src/app/api/donations/[id]/route.ts (PATCH, DELETE)
     - src/app/api/categories/[id]/route.ts (PATCH, DELETE)
     - src/app/api/events/route.ts (GET)
     - src/app/api/profile/me/route.ts (GET)
     - amend src/app/api/categories/route.ts to add POST
     - minor amend src/lib/categories-cache.ts invalidation hook

     Frontend (modified by FE agent):
     - src/app/(app)/layout.tsx — add prefetch
     - src/app/(app)/log/manual/page.tsx — wire submit
     - src/app/(app)/log/quick/page.tsx — wire sticky save bar + bulk POST
     - src/app/(app)/history/page.tsx — fetch events + Pacific bucketing
     - src/app/(app)/profile/page.tsx — wire range chips → fetch + aggregations
     - src/app/components/wellspring/shared.tsx — extend if a NewCategoryModal
     needs lifting
     - src/app/lib/api-client.ts — confirm endpoints (already typed, may need
     bulk-POST and PATCH/DELETE additions)

     Verification (acceptance for Phase 2)

     End-to-end flow on http://localhost:3000 with the running dev server (bg
     b6i9mp1n1):

     Out of scope

     - AI photo recognition (Phase 3)

  Phase 3 — Photo→AI flow + Reports + CSV

  Scope (3 endpoints + 3 screens, all shells already exist):

  Backend (src/lib/ai/gemini.ts + 3 new routes)

  1. POST /api/recognize — base64 in, RecognizedItem[] out. Build dynamic Gemini
   responseSchema with category enum from the active categories cache (60s);
  call gemini-2.5-flash; for each suggestion, fuzzy-match against
  itemCatalog.name + aliases (case-insensitive substring per CONTRACTS §4.5
  step 3) → on hit, snapshot categoryId/categoryName/programName + canonical
  name + defaultUnit + estimatedValue = qty × estimatedValuePerUnit; on miss,
  leave AI fields + warning: "not_in_catalog". Always 200 even at 0 matches.
  Errors: 400 INVALID_IMAGE, 502 AI_UNAVAILABLE, 429 RATE_LIMITED.
  2. GET /api/reports?from&to&groupBy=item|category|program — Mongo aggregation
  grouped by categoryId/programId/itemId internally (renames consolidate);
  response uses current names. Filters deleted: { $ne: true }. Returns
  ReportSummary with entryCount, totalValue, topItem, topCategory, rows[].
  3. GET /api/reports/csv?from&to — text/csv blob with Content-Disposition: 
  attachment; filename="wellspring-donations-YYYY-MM-DD-to-YYYY-MM-DD.csv"
  (Pacific dates). Header: Date,Item,Category,Program,Quantity,Unit,Estimated 
  Value,Source,Logged By,Notes. Sorted by donatedAt ASC. Uses snapshot names
  from each donation row (preserves historical categorization for tax filing).
  Source mapped to human labels: AI Photo, Quick Pick, Manual, Barcode.

  Frontend (3 page wirings + minor shared primitive)

  1. Photo capture (log/photo/page.tsx): <input type="file" accept="image/*" 
  capture="environment">; if HEIC → heic2any to JPEG; canvas-downscale longest
  edge to 2048; ≤5 MB; base64 → POST /api/recognize → spinner → write { items, 
  photoDataUrl } to sessionStorage → router push /log/review. On matchedCount 
  === 0 → toast "Could not match item to catalog. Try again or manually select."
   → push /log.
  2. AI Review (log/review/page.tsx): read sessionStorage; render one editable
  card per item with quantity stepper, unit dropdown, $ field, trash,
  CategoryDropdown, "+ New category", red "Not in catalog" chip when warning ===
   "not_in_catalog", amber "Edited" chip when locally changed. Save bar shows
  count + dollar total → apiClient.createDonations(items.map(... source: 
  "photo_ai")) → toast → /history. Discard → /log.
  3. Reports (reports/page.tsx): wire chips (This month / Last month / Q2 / YTD
  / Custom) computed in Pacific → apiClient.getReport({ from, to }). Mobile = 2
  stat cards + by-item table; iPad = 4 stat cards + table + top-5 horizontal bar
   (rows.slice(0,5), plain divs). Footer "Export CSV" →
  apiClient.downloadReportsCsv → URL.createObjectURL + click anchor.

  New deps the FE agent will install

  - heic2any (iPhone HEIC → JPEG; ~50KB gzip)

  Out of scope (Phase 4 if we get there)

  Empty/error-state polish, 1024×768 iPad AI Review tighter fit, Vercel Blob
  photo persistence (CONTRACTS §11 says MVP keeps photoUrl: null).

  Execution model (same as Phase 1+2)

  Two isolated worktrees → BE + FE agents run in parallel → I merge --no-ff in
  order BE then FE → tsc --noEmit clean → smoke-test endpoints → tag
  phase-3-complete + push.

  401 envelope unauthed

  worktrees, and spawn both agents in parallel.

     Photo page is unresponsive — diagnose + fix

     Context

     User just merged Phase 3 to main (commit dfc4c1b, ~10 minutes ago). On
     http://localhost:3000/log/photo they report: "I literally can't click any 
     of the UI elements. No clickable elements." Desktop browser, not mobile.

     This is exactly the symptom of being served the Phase 1 shell of
     src/app/(app)/log/photo/page.tsx, which had:
     - Drop zone rendered as a <Card> (a <div>) with no onClick → cursor stays
     default, page looks "not clickable"
     - "Open Camera" <PrimaryButton> with no onClick → clicks do nothing

     The Phase 3 merge replaced that with a fully wired client component (drop
     zone is a real <button onClick={openPicker}>, "Open Camera" has the same
     handler, both trigger a hidden <input type="file" capture="environment">).
     I just re-verified the file on disk at /mnt/c/Users/subha/desktop/projects/
     hackdavis-26/HackDavis2026/src/app/(app)/log/photo/page.tsx — it's the new
     wired version.

     The dev server (PID 33894, next-server v15.5.18 --turbopack, running
     uninterrupted since 03:27) is serving compiled chunks that predate the
     merge. WSL2 + Turbopack's filesystem watcher is known to miss change events
      when a long-running session has a wholesale file rewrite land via git 
     merge — the route stays cached on the previous bundle.

     The fix is to recycle the dev server so Turbopack recompiles /log/photo
     from the new source.

     Fix (one command)

     1. Kill the running Next dev process (PID 33894 + its parent npm/shell
     parents 33868, 33869) so all Turbopack workers release their cache.
     2. Start a fresh dev server in the background from the main worktree.
     3. Wait until /api/health returns 200 to confirm it's serving traffic.
     4. Have the user hard-reload /log/photo in the browser (Cmd/Ctrl+Shift+R)
     so the browser drops its bundle cache.

     If the restart doesn't fix it (fallback)

     After restart, if the user still sees a non-interactive page, the
     next-most-likely root causes (in order) are:

     1. Browser cache pinning the old _next/static/chunks URLs. Hard reload
     should fix; if not, open DevTools → Network → Disable cache → reload.
     2. Browser console error. Some import in the new page failing at runtime
     would freeze the React tree without crashing the dev overlay. Ask user to
     open DevTools console and read off the error. Most likely culprit if any:
     heic2any's dynamic import("heic2any") resolution under Turbopack.
     3. Hidden-input display:none blocking programmatic .click(). Modern desktop
      browsers all support this, but if the user is on a sandboxed Brave/Safari
     Tech Preview that blocks it, switch from className="hidden" to a
     sr-only-style positioning hack on the <input> in
     src/app/(app)/log/photo/page.tsx:191-198. (This is a 1-line change, not
     preemptively warranted.)
     4. <button> nesting accessibility violation. The drop zone <button>
     contains a <Subtle> which renders <span> — that's fine. No nested <button>
     inside <button>, which would cause React to silently drop click handlers.
     Verified during plan.

     Why no code change is the right call right now

     The new code at src/app/(app)/log/photo/page.tsx is correct. tsc --noEmit
     was clean before push, the integration smoke-tested 401 envelope on
     /api/recognize, and the page reads cleanly: <button type="button" 
     onClick={openPicker}> for the drop zone, <PrimaryButton type="button" 
     onClick={openPicker}> for the bottom CTA, both invoking
     inputRef.current?.click() against a hidden <input type="file" 
     accept="image/...,image/heic,image/heif" capture="environment"> whose
     onChange runs the heic→jpeg→downscale→base64→apiClient.recognizeImage
     pipeline. The bug is operational (stale dev bundle), not in the source. Do
     not preemptively refactor working code to chase a server-cache symptom.

     Critical files

     - src/app/(app)/log/photo/page.tsx — the wired page (read-only verification
      only; no edits planned).
     - src/app/components/wellspring/shared.tsx — exports Camera, Card, H2,
     PageHeader, PrimaryButton, Subtle, Toast, TopAppBar (verified at line
     1214–1230 for the icon re-export and earlier for the rest).
     - The running dev server: PID 33894 (and parents 33868, 33869).

     Verification (after restart)

     1. curl -fs http://localhost:3000/api/health returns 200 with
     {"ok":true,...}.
     2. Browser hard-reload of /log/photo shows: dashed-border drop zone with
     green leaf icon + "Tap to take a photo" + "or choose from gallery" + "Open
     Camera" button at bottom.
     3. Hover the drop zone — cursor turns to a pointer (it's a real <button>
     now).
     4. Click drop zone or "Open Camera" → native file picker opens.
     5. Pick a JPEG photo of a donation pile → loading overlay appears with
     "Recognizing…" → either lands on /log/review with editable rows OR pushes
     back to /log with the 0-match toast.

     - Refactoring to a <label htmlFor="..."> pattern preemptively — only do

     Photo flow redirect tweaks

     Context

     Two small behavior fixes after a real run-through of the AI photo flow:

     1. Save in AI Review currently redirects to /history — user wants /log (Log
      Home) instead. Demo flow is "log a batch, return to picking method," not
     "log a batch, jump to audit feed."
     2. 0-match on Photo currently shows a toast AND redirects to /log — user
     wants the toast to stay on the Photo screen so they can immediately retry
     with a different photo without an extra navigation step.

     Both are 1-line edits.

     Changes

     1. Review save → /log (not /history)

     File: src/app/(app)/log/review/page.tsx
     Line 255 — inside the handleSave success branch:

            sessionStorage.removeItem(STORAGE_KEY);
            const created = res.createdCount;
            setSuccessToast(`Saved ${created} donation${created === 1 ? "" : 
     "s"}`);
     -      router.push("/history");
     +      router.push("/log");

     Failure paths and the Discard button (handleDiscard at line 272) already
     push to /log, so this aligns the success path with the rest.

     2. 0-match on Photo → toast + stay (no redirect)

     File: src/app/(app)/log/photo/page.tsx
     Lines 156–161 — inside handleChange, the 0-match branch:

            if (result.matchedCount === 0) {
              setErrorToast("Could not match item to catalog. Try again or
     manually select.");
              reset();
     -        router.push("/log");
              return;
            }

     reset() already clears busy (so the buttons are clickable again) and clears
      inputRef.current.value (so the same file can be re-picked). The user sees
     the red toast on the Photo screen and can immediately tap the drop zone
     again.

     Verification

     After the edits, on http://localhost:3000:

     1. Save path: /log/photo → pick a recognized photo → land on /log/review →
     tap Save all → toast "Saved N donations" → land on /log (the 3-method
     picker), not /history.
     2. 0-match path: /log/photo → pick a photo that Gemini can't match (e.g., a
      wall, a face) → red toast "Could not match item to catalog. Try again or
     manually select." appears on the Photo screen → buttons are still active →
     tap drop zone again → file picker opens → retry.
     3. npx tsc --noEmit clean.
     4. No other behavior changes — Discard, Edit/Delete sheets, Quick Pick,
     Manual Entry, History, Profile all unchanged.

     Critical files

     - src/app/(app)/log/review/page.tsx — line 255 only.
     - src/app/(app)/log/photo/page.tsx — line 159 only (delete it).

     Out of scope

     - Changing the toast wording.

✻ Cogitated for 1m 0s

❯ Can you explain 3 a bit more. Specifically about structured logging           

● Structured logging = instead of console.log("user X did thing"), every log
  line is a JSON object with consistent fields (requestId, userId, route,
  durationMs, event, plus event-specific context). Vercel Functions auto-ingest
  stdout, so you can then filter logs like "all 500s on /api/recognize in the
  last hour, grouped by userId" — much more useful than scrolling free-text when
   something breaks.

  What I'd actually wire here: a tiny lib/logger.ts that writes JSON to stdout,
  used in every API route (/api/donations, /api/recognize, /api/reports) to log
  start + finish + errors with consistent fields. Maybe 30 minutes of work.

  The honest tradeoff for a hackathon: judges don't see logs, so it's invisible
  polish. The win is that if something dies during your demo, you can debug in
  10 seconds instead of 5 minutes. I'd skip it unless option 3 is what you want
  overall — for HackDavis specifically, option 1 (demo prep + polish) is usually
   higher leverage. Want me to do option 1 instead, or option 3 with structured
  logging included?

  The fastest path is the Vercel web UI — it auto-detects Next.js, wires the
  GitHub integration so future pushes auto-deploy, and the env-var setup is
  manual either way.

  Step-by-step:

  1. Go to https://vercel.com/new
  2. Import SubhanMNasir/HackDavis2026 (authorize the GitHub app if it's not
  already connected to your Vercel team)
  3. Leave framework preset as Next.js, root directory ./, default build command
  4. Environment Variables — add these four (paste the values from your local
  .env):

  | Key                               | Source                          |
  |-----------------------------------|---------------------------------|
  | NEXT_PUBLIC_CLERK_PUBLISHABLE_KEY | Clerk dashboard → API keys      |
  | CLERK_SECRET_KEY                  | Clerk dashboard → API keys      |
  | MONGODB_URI                       | Mongo Atlas → Connect → Drivers |
  | GOOGLE_API_KEY                    | Google AI Studio key for Gemini |

  4. Skip NEXT_PUBLIC_APP_URL — Vercel auto-injects it.
  5. Click Deploy. First build takes ~2 min.

  Two gotchas to check first:
  - Mongo Atlas IP allowlist — Vercel's runtime IPs aren't fixed. Either set the
   allowlist to 0.0.0.0/0 (simplest for hackathon) or use Atlas's Vercel
  integration. If this isn't done, every API call will hang and time out.
  - Clerk keys — if you're using pk_test_* (dev keys), they work on any URL. If
  you switched to pk_live_*, add your Vercel URL (*.vercel.app) to Clerk's
  allowed origins.

  Once it deploys, paste the URL back and I'll smoke-test the flow (sign in →
  log a donation → see it in history → reports). If anything breaks in prod, we
  fix it from there.

● That toast = HTTP 429 from Gemini (free-tier quota hit). Not a bug in our code
   — Google is throttling. Code path: src/lib/ai/gemini.ts:193-194.

  The free tier of gemini-2.5-flash has tight per-minute and per-day limits, so
  if you've been re-testing the photo flow repeatedly the bucket is now empty.

  Three options, easiest first:

  1. Just wait 60s and retry. Per-minute limits reset fast. If retries keep
  failing for >5 min, you've hit the daily cap (resets at Pacific midnight).
  2. Test the rest of the demo flow with Quick Pick + Manual — they don't burn
  AI quota and exercise everything except the recognize endpoint.
  3. Enable Google Cloud billing on the API key (Google AI Studio → API key →
  "Set up billing"). Bumps you to paid tier with much higher quotas. Survives
  the demo even under heavy retry.

  Want me to add a cheap mitigation? Two reasonable options:

  - In-memory dedup cache (hash → recognized items) — if you re-photograph the
  same items during testing, the second call returns instantly without a Gemini
  hit. Won't help with brand-new photos.
  - Swap default model to gemini-2.0-flash or gemini-2.5-flash-lite — separate
  quota bucket, slightly different result quality but usually fine for
  clearly-visible donation items.

  Which (if any) do you want?

❯ What is the cap                                                               

● Let me check Google's current published rate limits rather than guess from
  memory.

● Fetch(https://ai.google.dev/gemini-api/docs/rate-limits)
  ⎿  Received 94.6KB (200 OK)

● Fetch(https://ai.google.dev/gemini-api/docs/pricing)
  ⎿  Received 202.7KB (200 OK)

● Google has moved the exact numbers behind a per-account dashboard — they vary
  by region and account history now. The canonical answer is account-specific:

  Check your actual quota: https://aistudio.google.com/rate-limit (sign in with
  the same Google account that owns your GOOGLE_API_KEY).

  Approximate published baselines for free tier gemini-2.5-flash (from Google's
  recent docs and what surfaces on the AI Studio dashboard for most accounts):
  - ~10 requests / minute
  - ~250–500 requests / day
  - ~250K tokens / minute

  Paid Tier 1 (after enabling billing) jumps to ~1000 RPM and effectively no
  daily cap — typically the right move if you plan to demo more than ~5 photo
  runs in a session.

  If your dashboard still shows the daily bucket as exhausted, it resets at
  midnight Pacific. Per-minute resets in 60s.
